2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F_%C2%AB%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B7%D0%B5%C2%BB_(%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%B8,_%D0%BA%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D1%80.)102.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A health resort in
         <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">
          Sochi
         </a>
         , Russia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Black Sea
       </b>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Body_of_water" title="Body of water">
        body of water
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marginal_sea" title="Marginal sea">
        marginal sea
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       between
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">
        Eastern Europe
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">
        Caucasus
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">
        Western Asia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEP2001_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNEP2001-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is
       <a href="/wiki/Inflow_(hydrology)" title="Inflow (hydrology)">
        supplied by
       </a>
       a number of major rivers, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" title="Dnieper River">
        Dnieper
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Bug" title="Southern Bug">
        Southern Bug
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">
        Dniester
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Don_River_(Russia)" title="Don River (Russia)">
        Don
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Rioni_River" title="Rioni River">
        Rioni
       </a>
       . About a third of Europe drains into the Black Sea,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       including the countries of
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">
        Belarus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">
        Bosnia and Herzegovina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">
        Bulgaria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">
        Georgia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
        Germany
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">
        Moldova
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
        Serbia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">
        Slovakia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">
        Slovenia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Black Sea has an area of 436,400 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (168,500 sq mi) (not including the
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">
        Sea of Azov
       </a>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a maximum depth of 2,212 m (7,257 ft),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a volume of 547,000 km
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       (131,000 cu mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is constrained by the
       <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Mountains" title="Pontic Mountains">
        Pontic Mountains
       </a>
       to the south,
       <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">
        Caucasus Mountains
       </a>
       to the east,
       <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Mountains" title="Crimean Mountains">
        Crimean Mountains
       </a>
       to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Strandzha" title="Strandzha">
        Strandzha
       </a>
       to the southwest,
       <a href="/wiki/Dobrogea_Plateau" title="Dobrogea Plateau">
        Dobrogea Plateau
       </a>
       to the northwest, and features a wide shelf to the northwest. The longest east-west extent is about 1,175 km (730 mi).
      </p>
      <p>
       Important cities along the coast include
       <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">
        Batumi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Burgas" title="Burgas">
        Burgas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Constan%C8%9Ba" title="Constanța">
        Constanța
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Giresun" title="Giresun">
        Giresun
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">
        Istanbul
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kerch" title="Kerch">
        Kerch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Novorossiysk" title="Novorossiysk">
        Novorossiysk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">
        Odessa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ordu" title="Ordu">
        Ordu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Poti" title="Poti">
        Poti
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rize" title="Rize">
        Rize
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Samsun" title="Samsun">
        Samsun
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">
        Sevastopol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">
        Sochi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhumi" title="Sukhumi">
        Sukhumi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trabzon" title="Trabzon">
        Trabzon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">
        Varna
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">
        Yalta
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Zonguldak" title="Zonguldak">
        Zonguldak
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Black Sea has a positive
       <a href="/wiki/Water_balance" title="Water balance">
        water balance
       </a>
       ; that is, a net outflow of water 300 km
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       (72 cu mi) per year through the Bosphorus and the Dardanelles into the
       <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">
        Aegean Sea
       </a>
       . Mediterranean water flows into the Black Sea as part of a two-way hydrological exchange. The Black Sea outflow is cooler and less
       <a href="/wiki/Saline_water" title="Saline water">
        saline
       </a>
       , and floats over the warm, more saline Mediterranean inflow – as a result of differences in density caused by differences in salinity – leading to a significant
       <a href="/wiki/Anoxic_waters" title="Anoxic waters">
        anoxic
       </a>
       layer well below the surface waters. The Black Sea drains into the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       , via the Aegean Sea and various
       <a href="/wiki/Strait" title="Strait">
        straits
       </a>
       , and is navigable to the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">
        Bosphorus
       </a>
       Strait connects it to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">
        Sea of Marmara
       </a>
       , and the Strait of the
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       connects that sea to the Aegean Sea region of the Mediterranean. These waters separate Eastern Europe, the Caucasus and Western Asia. The Black Sea is also connected to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">
        Sea of Azov
       </a>
       by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strait_of_Kerch" title="Strait of Kerch">
        Strait of Kerch
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The water level has varied significantly. Due to these variations in the water level in the basin, the surrounding shelf and associated aprons have sometimes been land. At certain critical water levels it is possible for connections with surrounding water bodies to become established. It is through the most active of these connective routes, the
       <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Straits" title="Turkish Straits">
        Turkish Straits
       </a>
       , that the Black Sea joins the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_ocean" title="World ocean">
        world ocean
       </a>
       . When this hydrological link is not present, the Black Sea is an
       <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">
        endorheic basin
       </a>
       , operating independently of the global ocean system, like the
       <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">
        Caspian Sea
       </a>
       for example. Currently the Black Sea water level is relatively high, thus water is being exchanged with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       . The Turkish Straits connect the Black Sea with the Aegean Sea, and comprise the Bosphorus, the Sea of Marmara and the Dardanelles.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extent">
        Extent
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Extent">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">
        International Hydrographic Organization
       </a>
       defines the limits of the Black Sea as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <i>
           On the Southwest.
          </i>
          The Northeastern limit of the
          <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">
           Sea of Marmara
          </a>
          [A line joining
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Rumili" title="Cape Rumili">
           Cape Rumili
          </a>
          with
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Anatoli" title="Cape Anatoli">
           Cape Anatoli
          </a>
          (41°13'N)].
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <i>
           In the
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strait_of_Kerch" title="Strait of Kerch">
            Kertch Strait
           </a>
           .
          </i>
          A line joining Cape Takil and
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Panaghia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cape Panaghia (page does not exist)">
           Cape Panaghia
          </a>
          (45°02'N).
         </dd>
        </dl>
       </dd>
      </dl>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg/220px-Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg/330px-Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg/440px-Crimea_Laspi_Sunset.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
