      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_names">
        Modern names
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern names">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Current names of the sea are usually equivalents of the English name "Black Sea", including these given in the countries bordering the sea:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Abkhaz_language" title="Abkhaz language">
         Abkhaz language
        </a>
        Амшын Еиқәа,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [ɑmʂɨn ɛjkʷʰɑ]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Adyghe_language" title="Adyghe language">
         Adyghe language
        </a>
        Хы шӏуцӏэ,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [xə ʃʼəw.t͡sʼa]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">
         Bulgarian language
        </a>
        Черно море,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [ˈtʃɛrno moˈrɛ]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatar_language" title="Crimean Tatar language">
         Crimean Tatar language
        </a>
        Къара денъиз,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [qɑrɑ deŋiz]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">
         Georgian language
        </a>
        შავი ზღვა,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [ʃɑvi zɣvɑ]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Laz_language" title="Laz language">
         Laz
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Mingrelian_language" title="Mingrelian language">
         Mingrelian
        </a>
        languages - უჩა ზუღა,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [utʃɑ zuɣɑ]
         </a>
        </span>
        , or simply ზუღა,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [zuɣɑ]
         </a>
        </span>
        , "Sea"
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">
         Romanian language
        </a>
        Marea Neagră, (
        <small>
         pronounced
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [ˈmare̯a ˈne̯aɡrə]
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:Ro-Marea_Neagr%C4%83.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/Ro-Marea_Neagr%C4%83.ogg" title="Ro-Marea Neagră.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
         Russian language
        </a>
        Чёрное мо́рe,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [ˈtɕornəjə ˈmorʲə]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">
         Turkish language
        </a>
        Karadeniz,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [kaˈɾadeniz]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">
         Ukrainian language
        </a>
        Чорне море,
        <small>
         IPA:
        </small>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          [ˈtʃɔrnɛ ˈmɔrɛ]
         </a>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Such names have not yet been shown conclusively to predate the 13th century,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but there are indications that they may be considerably older.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       , the historical name "Euxine Sea", which holds a different meaning (see below), is still widely used:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
         Greek language
        </a>
        Éfxeinos Póntos (
        <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">
         Eύξεινος Πόντος
        </span>
        ); the literal Mavri Thalassa (
        <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">
         Μαύρη Θάλασσα
        </span>
        ) is less common
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The Black Sea is one of four seas named in English after common
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colour_term" title="Colour term">
        colour terms
       </a>
       —the others being the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
        Red Sea
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">
        White Sea
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Sea" title="Yellow Sea">
        Yellow Sea
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_names_and_etymology">
        Historical names and etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Historical names and etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The principal
       <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">
        Greek
       </a>
       name "Póntos Áxeinos" itself is generally accepted to be a rendering of
       <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">
        Iranian
       </a>
       <i>
        *axšaina-
       </i>
       (“dark colored”),
       <a href="/wiki/Cf." title="Cf.">
        cf.
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avestan_language" title="Avestan language">
        Avestan
       </a>
       <i>
        axšaēna-
       </i>
       (“dark colored”),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Persian_language" title="Old Persian language">
        Old Persian
       </a>
       <i>
        axšaina-
       </i>
       (color of
       <a href="/wiki/Turquoise" title="Turquoise">
        turquoise
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Persian_language" title="Middle Persian language">
        Middle Persian
       </a>
       <i>
        axšēn/xašēn
       </i>
       ("blue"), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Persian_language" title="New Persian language">
        New Persian
       </a>
       <i>
        xašīn
       </i>
       ("blue"), as well as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ossetic_language" title="Ossetic language">
        Ossetic
       </a>
       <i>
        œxsīn
       </i>
       (“dark gray").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ancient Greeks subsequently adopted the name, reportedly in all likelihood those who lived to the north of the Black Sea, and altered it into
       <i>
        á-xe(i)nos
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thereafter, Greek tradition refers to the Black Sea as the "Inhospitable Sea",
       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
        Πόντος Ἄξεινος
       </span>
       <i lang="grc-Latn" title="ISO 843 Greek (Ancient Greek language) transliteration" xml:lang="grc-Latn">
        Póntos Áxeinos
       </i>
       , first attested in
       <a href="/wiki/Pindar" title="Pindar">
        Pindar
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">
        c.
       </a>
       475 BC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The name, considered to be "ominous", was then later changed into the
       <a href="/wiki/Euphemism" title="Euphemism">
        euphemism
       </a>
       "Hospitable sea",
       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
        Εὔξεινος Πόντος
       </span>
       <i lang="grc-Latn" title="ISO 843 Greek (Ancient Greek language) transliteration" xml:lang="grc-Latn">
        Eúxeinos Póntos
       </i>
       , which was also for the first time attested in Pindar.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This became the commonly used designation in Greek for the sea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In contexts related to mythology, the older form "Póntos Áxeinos" remained favored.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Previously, it was erroneously suggested that the name had to be derived from the color of the water, or at least were to be related to climatic particulars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Black (or dark), in this context however, referred to a system in which colors represented the various "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_points" title="Cardinal points">
        cardinal points
       </a>
       " of the known world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Black, or dark represented the north, red the south, white for the west, and green or light blue for the east.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This symbolism based on cardinal points was used in a plethora of different occasions, and is therefore widely attested.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For example, the "Red Sea", a body of water reported since the time of
       <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">
        Herodotus
       </a>
       (
       <abbr title="circa">
        c.
       </abbr>
       484–c. 425 BC) in fact designated the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">
        Indian Ocean
       </a>
       , together with bodies of water known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">
        Persian Gulf
       </a>
       and the "actual"
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">
        Red Sea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the same explanation and reasoning, it is therefore considered to be impossible for the
       <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
        Scythians
       </a>
       (who principally roamed in what is present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       ) to have given the designation as they lived to the north of the sea, and it would be therefore a southern antipodal body of water for them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the name could have only been given by a people that were well aware of both the northern "black/dark" and southern "red" seas, it is therefore considered probable that it was given its name by the
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Achaemenids
       </a>
       (550–330 BC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">
        Strabo
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Geographica" title="Geographica">
         Geographica
        </a>
       </i>
       (1.2.10) reports that in antiquity, the Black Sea was often just called "the Sea" (
       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">
        ὁ πόντος
       </span>
       <i lang="grc-Latn" title="ISO 843 Greek (Ancient Greek language) transliteration" xml:lang="grc-Latn">
        ho pontos
       </i>
       ). He also thought that the Black Sea was called "inhospitable" before Greek colonization because it was difficult to navigate, and because its shores were inhabited by savage tribes.(7.3.6) The name was changed to "hospitable" after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milesians_(Greek)" title="Milesians (Greek)">
        Milesians
       </a>
       had colonized the southern shoreline, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pontus_(region)" title="Pontus (region)">
        Pontus
       </a>
       , making it part of Greek civilization.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Bundahishn" title="Bundahishn">
        Greater Bundahishn
       </a>
       , a sacred
       <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">
        Zoroastrian
       </a>
       text written in
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">
        Middle Persian
       </a>
       the Black Sea is called
       <i>
        Siyābun
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A map of Asia dating to 1570, entitled "Asiae Nova Descriptio", from
       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius" title="Abraham Ortelius">
        Abraham Ortelius
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Theatrum_Orbis_Terrarum" title="Theatrum Orbis Terrarum">
         Theatrum Orbis Terrarum
        </a>
       </i>
       , labels the sea
       <i>
        Mar Maggior
       </i>
       ("Great Sea", cf. Latin
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          mare major
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       English-language writers of the 18th century often used the name "Euxine Sea" (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">
            j
           </span>
           <span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">
            uː
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/j/: 'y' in 'yes'">
            j
           </span>
           <span title="/uː/: 'oo' in 'goose'">
            uː
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">
            aɪ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ) to refer to the Black Sea.
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Gibbon" title="Edward Gibbon">
        Edward Gibbon
       </a>
       , for instance, calls the sea by this name throughout
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_History_of_the_Decline_and_Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="The History of the Decline and Fall of the Roman Empire">
         The History of the Decline and Fall of the Roman Empire
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       period, the Black Sea was called either
       <i>
        Bahr-e Siyah
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Karadeniz
       </i>
       , both meaning "the Black Sea" in the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">
        Ottoman Turkish
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       It is worthy to note, that in the tenth-century geography book
       <a href="/wiki/Hudud_al-%27Alam" title="Hudud al-'Alam">
        Hudud al-'Alam
       </a>
       , written in the Persian language by an unknown author, the Black Sea is called "Georgian Sea", "Sea of Georgians" ("daryä-yi Gurziyan").
      </p>
      <p>
       Old
       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">
        Georgian
       </a>
       sources of 9th–14th centuries (
       <i>
        "
        <a href="/wiki/The_Georgian_Chronicles" title="The Georgian Chronicles">
         The Georgian Chronicles
        </a>
        "
       </i>
       ) were using the name "Speris Zğua" (სპერის ზღუა), which means "The Sea of Speri", after the name of
       <a href="/wiki/Kartvelian_peoples" title="Kartvelian peoples">
        Kartvelian
       </a>
       tribe Speris or
       <a href="/wiki/Saspers" title="Saspers">
        Saspers
       </a>
       , now in Turkey.
      </p>
      <p>
       The modern names of the Black Sea (
       <i>
        Chyornoye more
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Karadeniz
       </i>
       , etc.), stretch only back to the 13th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313_14-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmitt1989310–313-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_bathymetry">
        Geology and bathymetry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geology and bathymetry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="571" data-file-width="864" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg/220px-%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg/330px-%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg/440px-%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BA.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The bay of
         <a href="/wiki/Sudak" title="Sudak">
          Sudak
         </a>
         , Crimea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The geological origins of the basin can be traced back to two distinct relict
       <a href="/wiki/Back-arc_basin" title="Back-arc basin">
        back-arc basins
       </a>
       which were initiated by the splitting of an
       <a href="/wiki/Albian" title="Albian">
        Albian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_arc" title="Volcanic arc">
        volcanic arc
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Subduction" title="Subduction">
        subduction
       </a>
       of both the
       <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Tethys_Ocean" title="Paleo-Tethys Ocean">
        Paleo
       </a>
       - and Neo-
       <a href="/wiki/Tethys_Ocean" title="Tethys Ocean">
        Tethys
       </a>
       Oceans, but the timings of these events remain controversial.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since its initiation, compressional tectonic environments led to
       <a href="/wiki/Subsidence" title="Subsidence">
        subsidence
       </a>
       in the basin, interspersed with extensional phases resulting in large-scale
       <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">
        volcanism
       </a>
       and numerous
       <a href="/wiki/Orogeny" title="Orogeny">
        orogenies
       </a>
       , causing the uplift of the
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">
        Greater Caucasus
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontides" title="Pontides">
        Pontides
       </a>
       , Southern
       <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">
        Crimean Peninsula
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balkan" title="Balkan">
        Balkanides
       </a>
       mountain ranges.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The ongoing collision between the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">
        Eurasian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/African_Plate" title="African Plate">
        African
       </a>
       plates and westward escape of the
       <a href="/wiki/Anatolian_Plate" title="Anatolian Plate">
        Anatolian
       </a>
       block along the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Anatolian_Fault" title="North Anatolian Fault">
        North Anatolian Fault
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/East_Anatolian_Fault" title="East Anatolian Fault">
        East Anatolian Faults
       </a>
       dictates the current tectonic regime,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which features enhanced subsidence in the Black Sea basin and significant volcanic activity in the Anatolian region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is these geological mechanisms which, in the long term, have caused the periodic isolations of the Black Sea from the rest of the global ocean system.
      </p>
      <p>
       The modern basin is divided into two sub-basins by a convexity extending south from the
       <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">
        Crimean Peninsula
       </a>
       . The large shelf to the north of the basin is up to 190 km (120 mi) wide, and features a shallow apron with gradients between 1:40 and 1:1000. The southern edge around Turkey and the eastern edge around
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">
        Georgia
       </a>
       , however, are typified by a narrow shelf that rarely exceeds 20 km (12 mi) in width and a steep apron that is typically 1:40 gradient with numerous submarine canyons and channel extensions. The
       <a href="/wiki/Euxine_abyssal_plain" title="Euxine abyssal plain">
        Euxine abyssal plain
       </a>
       in the centre of the Black Sea reaches a maximum depth of 2,212 metres (7,257.22 feet) just south of
       <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">
        Yalta
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">
        Crimean Peninsula
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Littoral_zone" title="Littoral zone">
        littoral zone
       </a>
       of the Black Sea is often referred to as the
       <b>
        Pontic littoral
       </b>
       or
       <b>
        Pontic zone
       </b>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prothero1_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Prothero1-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The area surrounding the Black Sea is commonly referred to as the
       <i>
        Black Sea Region
       </i>
       . Its northern part lies within the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Chernozem" title="Chernozem">
         Chernozem
        </a>
        belt
       </i>
       (black soil belt) which goes from eastern Croatia (
       <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">
        Slavonia
       </a>
       ), along the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       (northern Serbia, northern Bulgaria (
       <a href="/wiki/Danubian_Plain_(Bulgaria)" title="Danubian Plain (Bulgaria)">
        Danubian Plain
       </a>
       ) and southern Romania (
       <a href="/wiki/Wallachian_Plain" title="Wallachian Plain">
        Wallachian Plain
       </a>
       )) to northeast Ukraine and further across the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Black_Earth_Region" title="Central Black Earth Region">
        Central Black Earth Region
       </a>
       and southern Russia into
       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">
        Siberia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrology">
        Hydrology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hydrology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1865" data-file-width="2080" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg/300px-The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg/450px-The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg/600px-The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Danube_Spills_into_the_Black_Sea.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         This
         <a href="/wiki/SeaWiFS" title="SeaWiFS">
          SeaWiFS
         </a>
         view reveals the colourful interplay of currents on the sea's surface
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Black Sea is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marginal_sea" title="Marginal sea">
        marginal sea
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is the world's largest body of water with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meromictic" title="Meromictic">
        meromictic
       </a>
       basin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merriam_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Merriam-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The deep waters do not mix with the upper layers of water that receive oxygen from the atmosphere. As a result, over 90% of the deeper Black Sea volume is
       <a href="/wiki/Anoxic_waters" title="Anoxic waters">
        anoxic
       </a>
       water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exploring_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Exploring-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Black Sea's circulation patterns are primarily controlled by basin topography and
       <a href="/wiki/Fluvial" title="Fluvial">
        fluvial
       </a>
       inputs, which result in a strongly stratified vertical structure. Because of the extreme stratification, it is classified as a
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary#Salt_wedge" title="Estuary">
        salt wedge estuary
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Black Sea only experiences water transfer with the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       , so all inflow and outflow occurs in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">
        Bosphorus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       . Inflow from the Mediterranean has a higher salinity and density than the outflow, creating the classical estuarine circulation. This means that inflow of dense water from the Mediterranean occurs at the bottom of the basin while outflow of fresher Black Sea surface-water into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marmara_Sea" title="Marmara Sea">
        Marmara Sea
       </a>
       occurs near the surface. Fresher surface water is the product of the fluvial inputs, and this makes the Black Sea a positive sea. The net input of freshwater creates an outflow volume about twice that of the inflow. Evaporation and precipitation are roughly equal at about 300 cubic kilometres per year (72 cu mi/a).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of the narrowness and shallowness of the Bosphorus and Dardanelles (their respective depths are only 33 and 70 meters), inflow and outflow current speeds are high and there is significant vertical shear. This allows for turbulent mixing of the two layers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Surface water leaves the Black Sea with a salinity of 17
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Practical_salinity_unit" title="Practical salinity unit">
        psu
       </a>
       and reaches the Mediterranean with a salinity of 34 psu. Likewise, inflow of the Mediterranean with salinity 38.5 psu experiences a decrease to about 34 psu.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Mean surface circulation is
       <a href="/wiki/Cyclonic_rotation" title="Cyclonic rotation">
        cyclonic
       </a>
       and waters around the perimeter of the Black Sea circulate in a basin-wide shelfbreak
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gyre" title="Gyre">
        gyre
       </a>
       known as the Rim Current. The Rim Current has a maximum velocity of about 50–100 cm/s. Within this feature, two smaller cyclonic gyres operate, occupying the eastern and western sectors of the basin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Eastern and Western Gyres are well-organized systems in the winter but dissipate into a series of interconnected
       <a href="/wiki/Eddy_(fluid_dynamics)" title="Eddy (fluid dynamics)">
        eddies
       </a>
       in the summer and autumn. Mesoscale activity in the peripheral flow becomes more pronounced during these warmer seasons and is subject to interannual variability.
      </p>
      <p>
       Outside of the Rim Current, numerous quasi-permanent coastal eddies are formed as a result of upwelling around the coastal apron and "wind curl" mechanisms. The intra-annual strength of these features is controlled by seasonal atmospheric and fluvial variations. During the spring, the Batumi eddy forms in the southeastern corner of the sea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korotaev_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Korotaev-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Beneath the surface waters—from about 50–100 meters—there exists a
       <a href="/wiki/Halocline" title="Halocline">
        halocline
       </a>
       that stops at the Cold Intermediate Layer (CIL). This layer is composed of cool, salty surface waters, which are the result of localized atmospheric cooling and decreased fluvial input during the winter months. It is the remnant of the winter surface mixed layer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The base of the CIL is marked by a major
       <a href="/wiki/Pycnocline" title="Pycnocline">
        pycnocline
       </a>
       at about 100–200 metres (330–660 ft) and this density disparity is the major mechanism for isolation of the deep water.
      </p>
      <p>
       Below the pycnocline is the Deep Water mass, where salinity increases to 22.3 psu and temperatures rise to around 8.9 °C.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Talley_24-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Talley-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The hydrochemical environment shifts from oxygenated to anoxic, as bacterial decomposition of sunken biomass utilizes all of the free oxygen. Weak
       <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_heating" title="Geothermal heating">
        geothermal heating
       </a>
       and long
       <a href="/wiki/Residence_time_(fluid_dynamics)" title="Residence time (fluid dynamics)">
        residence time
       </a>
       create a very thick convective bottom layer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korotaev_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Korotaev-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrochemistry">
        Hydrochemistry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hydrochemistry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Because of the anoxic water at depth, organic matter, including
       <a href="/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_environment" title="Human impact on the environment">
        anthropogenic
       </a>
       artifacts such as boat hulls, are well preserved. During periods of high surface productivity, short-lived
       <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">
        algal
       </a>
       blooms form organic rich layers known as
       <a href="/wiki/Sapropel" title="Sapropel">
        sapropels
       </a>
       . Scientists have reported an annual
       <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">
        phytoplankton
       </a>
       bloom that can be seen in many NASA images of the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result of these characteristics the Black Sea has gained interest from the field of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_archaeology" title="Marine archaeology">
        marine archaeology
       </a>
       as ancient shipwrecks in excellent states of preservation have been discovered, such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">
        Byzantine
       </a>
       wreck
       <a href="/wiki/Sinop_D" title="Sinop D">
        Sinop D
       </a>
       , located in the anoxic layer off the coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Sinop,_Turkey" title="Sinop, Turkey">
        Sinop, Turkey
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Modelling shows the release of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">
        hydrogen sulfide
       </a>
       clouds in the event of an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asteroid_impact" title="Asteroid impact">
        asteroid impact
       </a>
       into the Black Sea would pose a threat to health—or even life—for people living on the Black Sea coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There have been isolated reports of flares on the Black Sea occurring during thunderstorms, possibly caused by lightning igniting combustible gas seeping up from the sea depths.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ecology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Marine">
        Marine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Marine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_fish_of_the_Black_Sea" title="List of fish of the Black Sea">
        List of fish of the Black Sea
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:POTI.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2128" data-file-width="2832" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/POTI.JPG/220px-POTI.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/POTI.JPG/330px-POTI.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/POTI.JPG/440px-POTI.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:POTI.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The port of
         <a href="/wiki/Poti" title="Poti">
          Poti
         </a>
         , Georgia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Black Sea supports an active and dynamic marine ecosystem, dominated by species suited to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brackish" title="Brackish">
        brackish
       </a>
       , nutrient-rich, conditions. As with all marine food webs, the Black Sea features a range of
       <a href="/wiki/Trophic_level" title="Trophic level">
        trophic
       </a>
       groups, with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autotrophic" title="Autotrophic">
        autotrophic
       </a>
       algae, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diatoms" title="Diatoms">
        diatoms
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dinoflagellates" title="Dinoflagellates">
        dinoflagellates
       </a>
       , acting as primary producers. The fluvial systems draining Eurasia and central Europe introduce large volumes of sediment and dissolved nutrients into the Black Sea, but distribution of these nutrients is controlled by the degree of physiochemical stratification, which is, in turn, dictated by seasonal physiographic development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz99_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Oguz99-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During winter, strong wind promotes convective overturning and upwelling of nutrients, while high summer temperatures result in a marked vertical stratification and a warm, shallow mixed layer.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Oguz-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Day length and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insolation" title="Insolation">
        insolation
       </a>
       intensity also controls the extent of the
       <a href="/wiki/Photic_zone" title="Photic zone">
        photic zone
       </a>
       . Subsurface productivity is limited by nutrient availability, as the anoxic bottom waters act as a sink for reduced nitrate, in the form of ammonia. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benthic" title="Benthic">
        benthic
       </a>
       zone also plays an important role in Black Sea nutrient cycling, as chemosynthetic organisms and anoxic geochemical pathways recycle nutrients which can be upwelled to the photic zone, enhancing productivity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In total, Black Sea's biodiversity contains around one-third of Mediterranean's, and is experiencing natural and artificial invasions or Mediterranizations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phytoplankton">
        Phytoplankton
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Phytoplankton">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3600" data-file-width="4800" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg/300px-Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg/450px-Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg/600px-Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_Sea_Nasa_May_25_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">
          Phytoplankton
         </a>
         blooms and plumes of sediment form the bright blue swirls that ring the Black Sea in this 2004 image
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The main phytoplankton groups present in the Black Sea are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dinoflagellates" title="Dinoflagellates">
        dinoflagellates
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diatoms" title="Diatoms">
        diatoms
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coccolithophores" title="Coccolithophores">
        coccolithophores
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">
        cyanobacteria
       </a>
       . Generally, the annual cycle of phytoplankton development comprises significant diatom and dinoflagellate-dominated spring production, followed by a weaker mixed assemblage of community development below the seasonal thermocline during summer months and a surface-intensified autumn production.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Oguz-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This pattern of productivity is also augmented by an
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Emiliania_huxleyi" title="Emiliania huxleyi">
         Emiliania huxleyi
        </a>
       </i>
       bloom during the late spring and summer months.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dinoflagellates" title="Dinoflagellates">
         Dinoflagellates
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Annual dinoflagellate distribution is defined by an extended bloom period in subsurface waters during the late spring and summer. In November, subsurface plankton production is combined with surface production, due to vertical mixing of water masses and nutrients such as
        <a href="/wiki/Nitrite" title="Nitrite">
         nitrite
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz99_31-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Oguz99-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The major bloom-forming dinoflagellate species in the Black Sea is
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Gymnodinium" title="Gymnodinium">
          Gymnodinium
         </a>
        </i>
        sp.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eker-Develi,_E_2003_37-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Eker-Develi,_E_2003-37">
          [37]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Estimates of dinoflagellate diversity in the Black Sea range from 193
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
         <a href="#cite_note-38">
          [38]
         </a>
        </sup>
        to 267 species.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomez_39-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gomez-39">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
        This level of species richness is relatively low in comparison to the Mediterranean Sea, which is attributable to the brackish conditions, low water transparency and presence of
        <a href="/wiki/Anoxic_waters" title="Anoxic waters">
         anoxic
        </a>
        bottom waters. It is also possible that the low winter temperatures below 4 °C (39 °F) of the Black Sea prevent
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermophilous" title="Thermophilous">
         thermophilous
        </a>
        species from becoming established. The relatively high organic matter content of Black Sea surface water favour the development of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heterotrophic" title="Heterotrophic">
         heterotrophic
        </a>
        (an organism which uses organic carbon for growth) and mixotrophic dinoflagellates species (able to exploit different trophic pathways), relative to autotrophs. Despite its unique hydrographic setting, there are no confirmed
        <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">
         endemic
        </a>
        dinoflagellate species in the Black Sea.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gomez_39-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gomez-39">
          [39]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diatoms" title="Diatoms">
         Diatoms
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        The Black Sea is populated by many species of marine diatom, which commonly exist as colonies of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicellular" title="Unicellular">
         unicellular
        </a>
        , non-motile auto- and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heterotrophic" title="Heterotrophic">
         heterotrophic
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">
         algae
        </a>
        . The life-cycle of most diatoms can be described as 'boom and bust' and the Black Sea is no exception, with diatom blooms occurring in surface waters throughout the year, most reliably during March.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz99_31-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Oguz99-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In simple terms, the phase of rapid population growth in diatoms is caused by the in-wash of
        <a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">
         silicon
        </a>
        -bearing terrestrial sediments, and when the supply of silicon is exhausted, the diatoms begin to sink out of the photic zone and produce resting
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cysts" title="Cysts">
         cysts
        </a>
        . Additional factors such as predation by zooplankton and
        <a href="/wiki/Ammonium" title="Ammonium">
         ammonium
        </a>
        -based regenerated production also have a role to play in the annual diatom cycle.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz99_31-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-Oguz99-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oguz_32-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-Oguz-32">
          [32]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Typically,
        <i>
         <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
          <i>
           Proboscia alata
          </i>
         </span>
        </i>
        blooms during spring and
        <i>
         <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
          <i>
           Pseudosolenia calcar-avis
          </i>
         </span>
        </i>
        blooms during the autumn.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eker-Develi,_E_2003_37-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Eker-Develi,_E_2003-37">
          [37]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coccolithophores" title="Coccolithophores">
         Coccolithophores
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Coccolithophores are a type of
        <a href="/wiki/Motility" title="Motility">
         motile
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autotrophic" title="Autotrophic">
         autotrophic
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">
         phytoplankton
        </a>
        that produce CaCO
        <sub>
         3
        </sub>
        plates, known as
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coccoliths" title="Coccoliths">
         coccoliths
        </a>
        , as part of their life cycle. In the Black Sea, the main period of
        <a href="/wiki/Coccolithophore" title="Coccolithophore">
         coccolithophore
        </a>
        growth occurs after the bulk of the dinoflagellate growth has taken place. In May, the dinoflagellates move below the seasonal
        <a href="/wiki/Thermocline" title="Thermocline">
         thermocline
        </a>
        , into deeper waters, where more nutrients are available. This permits coccolithophores to utilise the nutrients in the upper waters, and by the end of May, with favourable light and temperature conditions, growth rates reach their highest. The major bloom forming species is
        <i>
         <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Emiliania_huxleyi" title="Emiliania huxleyi">
            Emiliania huxleyi
           </a>
          </i>
         </span>
        </i>
        , which is also responsible for the release of
        <a href="/wiki/Dimethyl_sulfide" title="Dimethyl sulfide">
         dimethyl sulfide
        </a>
        into the atmosphere. Overall, coccolithophore diversity is low in the Black Sea, and although recent sediments are dominated by
        <i>
         <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
          <i>
           E. huxleyi
          </i>
         </span>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
          <i>
           Braarudosphaera bigelowii
          </i>
         </span>
        </i>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">
         Holocene
        </a>
        sediments have also been shown to contain Helicopondosphaera and Discolithina species.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cyanobacteria" title="Cyanobacteria">
         Cyanobacteria
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Cyanobacteria are a phylum of
        <a href="/wiki/Picoplankton" title="Picoplankton">
         picoplanktonic
        </a>
        (plankton ranging in size from 0.2 to 2.0
        <a href="/wiki/Micrometre" title="Micrometre">
         µm
        </a>
        )
        <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">
         bacteria
        </a>
        that obtain their energy via
        <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">
         photosynthesis
        </a>
        , and are present throughout the world's oceans. They exhibit a range of morphologiies, including filamentous colonies and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biofilms" title="Biofilms">
         biofilms
        </a>
        . In the Black Sea, several species are present, and as an example,
        <i>
         Synechococcus
        </i>
        spp. can be found throughout the photic zone, although concentration decreases with increasing depth. Other factors which exert an influence on distribution include nutrient availability, predation and salinity.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
         <a href="#cite_note-40">
          [40]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_species">
        Animal species
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Animal species">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Zebra_mussel" title="Zebra mussel">
         Zebra mussel
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        The Black Sea along with the
        <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">
         Caspian Sea
        </a>
        is part of the Zebra mussel's native range. The mussel has been accidentally introduced around the world and become an
        <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">
         invasive species
        </a>
        where it has been introduced.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_Carp" title="Common Carp">
         Common Carp
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        The Common Carp's native range extends to The Black Sea along with the Caspian Sea and
        <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">
         Aral Sea
        </a>
        . Like the Zebra mussel the Common Carp is an invasive species when introduced to other habitats.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Round_Goby" title="Round Goby">
         Round Goby
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Is another native fish that is also found in the Caspian Sea. It preys upon Zebra mussels. Like the mussels and common carp it has become invasive when introduced to other environments, like the
        <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">
         Great Lakes
        </a>
        .
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Marine Mammals and marine
        <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">
         megafaunas
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        Marine mammals present within the basin include two species of dolphins (
        <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">
         common
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
         <a href="#cite_note-41">
          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">
         bottlenose
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
         <a href="#cite_note-42">
          [42]
         </a>
        </sup>
        ) and
        <a href="/wiki/Harbour_porpoise" title="Harbour porpoise">
         harbour porpoise
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
         <a href="#cite_note-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
        inhabit the sea although all of these are endangered due to pressures and impacts by human activities. All the three species have been classified as a distinct subspecies from those in the Mediterranean and in Atlantic Seas and endemic to Black and Azov Seas, and are more active during nights in Turkish Straits.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Risso's_44-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Risso's-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
        However, construction of the
        <a href="/wiki/Kerch_Strait_Bridge" title="Kerch Strait Bridge">
         Kerch Strait Bridge
        </a>
        caused increases in nutrients and planktons in the waters, attracting large numbers of fish and more than 1,000 of bottlenose dolphins.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
         <a href="#cite_note-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
        On the other hand, however, others claim that construction may cause devastating damages on ecosystem including dolphins.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
         <a href="#cite_note-46">
          [46]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        Critically endangered
        <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_monk_seal" title="Mediterranean monk seal">
         Mediterranean monk seals
        </a>
        were historically abundant in Black Sea, and are regarded to have become extinct from the basin since in 1997.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iucn_47-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-iucn-47">
          [47]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Monk seals were present at the
        <a href="/wiki/Snake_Island_(Black_Sea)" title="Snake Island (Black Sea)">
         Snake Island
        </a>
        until 1950s, and several locations such as the
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Danube_Plavni_Nature_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Danube Plavni Nature Reserve (page does not exist)">
         Danube Plavni Nature Reserve
        </a>
        <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
         (
         <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%94%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%B9%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%84%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA" title="ru:Дунайский биосферный заповедник">
          ru
         </a>
         )
        </span>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Do%C4%9Fankent" title="Doğankent">
         Doğankent
        </a>
        were last of
        <a href="/wiki/Hauling-out" title="Hauling-out">
         hauling-out
        </a>
        sites in post-1990.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlackPedia_48-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-BlackPedia-48">
          [48]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Very few animals still thrive in the
        <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Marmara" title="Sea of Marmara">
         Sea of Marmara
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
         <a href="#cite_note-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
       <dd>
        Ongoing Mediterranizations may or may not boost in increases of cetacean diversity in Turkish Straits
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Risso's_44-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Risso's-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
        hence in Black and Azov basins.
       </dd>
       <dd>
        Various species of
        <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">
         pinnipeds
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Sea_otter" title="Sea otter">
         sea otter
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Beluga_whale" title="Beluga whale">
         beluga whales
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreekCetacea_50-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-GreekCetacea-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
         <a href="#cite_note-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
        were introduced into the Black Sea by mankind and later escaped either by accidental or purported causes. Of these,
        <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">
         grey seal
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
         <a href="#cite_note-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and beluga whales
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreekCetacea_50-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-GreekCetacea-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
        have been recorded with successful, long-term occurrences.
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Great_white_shark" title="Great white shark">
         Great white sharks
        </a>
        are known to reach into the Sea of Marmara and Bosphorus Strait and
        <a href="/wiki/Basking_shark" title="Basking shark">
         basking shark
        </a>
        into Dardanelles although it is unclear whether or not these sharks may reach into the Black and Azov basins.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
         <a href="#cite_note-53">
          [53]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
         <a href="#cite_note-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:269px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dolphins_swim_near_ferry_in_port_of_Batumi_150505-A-PU919-7446.jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">

         </div>
         Common dolphins
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cetacean_surfacing_behavior" title="Cetacean surfacing behavior">
          porpoising
         </a>
         with a ferry at
         <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">
          Batumi
         </a>
         port
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_effects_of_pollution">
        Ecological effects of pollution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ecological effects of pollution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Since the 1960s, rapid industrial expansion along the Black Sea coast line and the construction of a major dam has significantly increased annual variability in the N:P:Si ratio in the basin. In coastal areas, the biological effect of these changes has been an increase in the frequency of monospecific phytoplankton blooms, with diatom bloom frequency increasing by a factor of 2.5 and non-diatom bloom frequency increasing by a factor of 6. The non-diatoms, such as the prymnesiophytes
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          Emiliania huxleyi
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       (coccolithophore),
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          Chromulina
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       sp., and the Euglenophyte
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          Eutreptia lanowii
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       are able to out-compete diatom species because of the limited availability of Si, a necessary constituent of diatom frustules.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a consequence of these blooms, benthic macrophyte populations were deprived of light, while anoxia caused mass mortality in marine animals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The decline in macrophytes was further compounded by overfishing during the 1970s, while the invasive ctenophore
       <i>
        Mnemiopsis
       </i>
       reduced the biomass of copepods and other zooplankton in the late 1980s. Additionally, an alien species—the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warty_comb_jelly" title="Warty comb jelly">
        warty comb jelly
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          Mnemiopsis leidyi
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       )—was able to establish itself in the basin, exploding from a few individuals to an estimated biomass of one billion metric tons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The change in species composition in Black Sea waters also has consequences for hydrochemistry, as Ca-producing coccolithophores influence salinity and pH, although these ramifications have yet to be fully quantified. In central Black Sea waters, Si levels were also significantly reduced, due to a decrease in the flux of Si associated with advection across isopycnal surfaces. This phenomenon demonstrates the potential for localised alterations in Black Sea nutrient input to have basin-wide effects.
      </p>
      <p>
       Pollution reduction and regulation efforts have led to a partial recovery of the Black Sea ecosystem during the 1990s, and an EU monitoring exercise, 'EROS21', revealed decreased N and P values, relative to the 1989 peak.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Recently, scientists have noted signs of ecological recovery, in part due to the construction of new sewage treatment plants in Slovakia, Hungary, Romania, and Bulgaria in connection with membership in the European Union.
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          Mnemiopsis leidyi
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       populations have been checked with the arrival of another alien species which feeds on them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 82px">
        <div style="width: 82px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 80px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="402" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg/120px-Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg/181px-Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg/241px-Black_sea_fauna_jelly_01.jpg 2x" width="80"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Jellyfish" title="Jellyfish">
            Jellyfish
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 122px">
        <div style="width: 122px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 120px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="596" data-file-width="596" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg/180px-Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg/270px-Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg/360px-Black_sea_fauna_actinia_01.jpg 2x" width="120"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Actiniaria" title="Actiniaria">
            Actinia
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 122px">
        <div style="width: 122px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 120px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_sea_fauna_actinia_02.JPG">

          </p>
