      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terrestrial">
        Terrestrial
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terrestrial">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG/220px-On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG/330px-On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG/440px-On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:On_the_way_to_Akhun_mountain.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Statues of a man and a
         <a href="/wiki/Tiger" title="Tiger">
          tiger
         </a>
         , on the way to
         <a href="/wiki/Mount_Akhun" title="Mount Akhun">
          Mount Akhun
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the past, the range of the
       <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_lion" title="Asiatic lion">
        Asiatic lion
       </a>
       extended from
       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
        South Asia
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
        Balkans
       </a>
       , possibly up to the Danube. Places like Turkey and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Caucasus" title="Trans-Caucasus">
        Trans-Caucasus
       </a>
       were in this range. The
       <a href="/wiki/Caspian_tiger" title="Caspian tiger">
        Caspian tiger
       </a>
       occurred in
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Anatolia_Region" title="Eastern Anatolia Region">
        eastern Turkey
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">
        Caucasus
       </a>
       , at least. The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tiger_versus_lion#Asiatic_lions_and_Caspian_tigers" title="Tiger versus lion">
         lyuti zver
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Russian_language" title="Old Russian language">
        Old Russian
       </a>
       for "fierce animal") that was encountered by
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_II_Monomakh" title="Vladimir II Monomakh">
        Vladimir II Monomakh
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Velikiy_Kniaz" title="Velikiy Kniaz">
        Velikiy Kniaz
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">
        Kievan Rus'
       </a>
       (which ranged to the Black Sea in the south),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encyclopediaofukraine_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-encyclopediaofukraine-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       may have been a tiger or
       <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">
        leopard
       </a>
       , rather than a
       <a href="/wiki/Steppe_wolf" title="Steppe wolf">
        wolf
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">
        lynx
       </a>
       , due to the way it behaved towards him and his
       <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">
        horse
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geptner1972_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geptner1972-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg/220px-Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg/330px-Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg/440px-Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ice_on_the_Gulf_of_Odessa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The ice on the
         <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Odessa" title="Gulf of Odessa">
          Gulf of Odessa
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Short-term climatic variation in the Black Sea region is significantly influenced by the operation of the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_oscillation" title="North Atlantic oscillation">
        North Atlantic oscillation
       </a>
       , the climatic mechanisms resulting from the interaction between the north Atlantic and mid-latitude air masses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While the exact mechanisms causing the North Atlantic Oscillation remain unclear,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it is thought the climate conditions established in western Europe mediate the heat and precipitation fluxes reaching Central Europe and Eurasia, regulating the formation of winter
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclones" title="Cyclones">
        cyclones
       </a>
       , which are largely responsible for regional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">
        precipitation
       </a>
       inputs
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and influence Mediterranean Sea Surface Temperatures (SST's).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The relative strength of these systems also limits the amount of cold air arriving from northern regions during winter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Other influencing factors include the regional
       <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">
        topography
       </a>
       , as depressions and storms systems arriving from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       are funneled through the low land around the Bosphorus,
       <a href="/wiki/Pontic_Mountains" title="Pontic Mountains">
        Pontic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">
        Caucasus
       </a>
       mountain ranges acting as wave guides, limiting the speed and paths of cyclones passing through the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">
        Islands
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Islands">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (January 2018)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>

           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       There are some islands in the Black sea that belong to Bulgaria, Romania, Turkey, and Ukraine:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        St.Thomas Island - Bulgaria
       </li>
       <li>
        St.Anastasia Island - Bulgaria
       </li>
       <li>
        St.Cyricus Island - Bulgaria
       </li>
       <li>
        St.Ivan Island - Bulgaria
       </li>
       <li>
        St.Peter Island - Bulgaria
       </li>
       <li>
        Sacalinu Mare Island - Romania
       </li>
       <li>
        Sacalinu Mic Island - Romania
       </li>
       <li>
        Novaya Zemliya - Romania
       </li>
       <li>
        Utrish Island
       </li>
       <li>
        Krupinin Island
       </li>
       <li>
        Sudiuk Island
       </li>
       <li>
        Kefken Island
       </li>
       <li>
        Oreke Island
       </li>
       <li>
        Giresun Island
       </li>
       <li>
        Dzharylgach Island - Ukraine
       </li>
       <li>
        Zmiinyi (Snake) Island - Ukraine
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mediterranean_connection_during_the_Holocene">
        Mediterranean connection during the Holocene
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mediterranean connection during the Holocene">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1163" data-file-width="1000" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg/170px-Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg/255px-Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg/340px-Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Istanbul_and_Bosporus_big.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">
          Bosphorus
         </a>
         , taken from the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
          International Space Station
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dardanelles_map2.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="700" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Dardanelles_map2.png/300px-Dardanelles_map2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Dardanelles_map2.png/450px-Dardanelles_map2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Dardanelles_map2.png/600px-Dardanelles_map2.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dardanelles_map2.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the
         <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
          Dardanelles
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Black Sea is connected to the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Ocean" title="World Ocean">
        World Ocean
       </a>
       by a chain of two shallow straits, the
       <a href="/wiki/Dardanelles" title="Dardanelles">
        Dardanelles
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">
        Bosphorus
       </a>
       . The Dardanelles is 55 m (180 ft) deep and the Bosphorus is as shallow as 36 m (118 ft). By comparison, at the height of the last
       <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">
        ice age
       </a>
       , sea levels were more than 100 m (330 ft) lower than they are now.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also evidence that water levels in the Black Sea were considerably lower at some point during the post-glacial period. Some researchers theorize that the Black Sea had been a landlocked freshwater lake (at least in upper layers) during the last glaciation and for some time after.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the aftermath of the last glacial period, water levels in the Black Sea and the Aegean Sea rose independently until they were high enough to exchange water. The exact timeline of this development is still subject to debate. One possibility is that the Black Sea filled first, with excess fresh water flowing over the Bosphorus sill and eventually into the Mediterranean Sea. There are also catastrophic scenarios, such as the "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Sea_deluge_theory" title="Black Sea deluge theory">
        Black Sea deluge theory
       </a>
       " put forward by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=William_Ryan_(geologist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="William Ryan (geologist) (page does not exist)">
        William Ryan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walter_Pitman_(geologist)" title="Walter Pitman (geologist)">
        Walter Pitman
       </a>
       and
       <a class="extiw" href="https://bg.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%94%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2" title="bg:Петко Димитров">
        Petko Dimitrov
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Deluge_hypothesis">
        Deluge hypothesis
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Deluge hypothesis">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea_deluge_hypothesis" title="Black Sea deluge hypothesis">
        Black Sea deluge hypothesis
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Black Sea deluge
       </b>
       is a hypothesized catastrophic rise in the level of the Black Sea circa 5600 BC due to waters from the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       breaching a sill in the
       <a href="/wiki/Bosporus" title="Bosporus">
        Bosporus
       </a>
       Strait. The hypothesis was headlined when
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">
         The New York Times
        </a>
       </i>
       published it in December 1996, shortly before it was published in an
       <a href="/wiki/Academic_journal" title="Academic journal">
        academic journal
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While it is agreed that the sequence of events described did occur, there is debate over the suddenness, dating and magnitude of the events. Relevant to the hypothesis is that its description has led some to connect this catastrophe with prehistoric
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deluge_(mythology)" title="Deluge (mythology)">
        flood myths
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recorded_history">
        Recorded history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Recorded history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2180" data-file-width="2900" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg/300px-Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg/450px-Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg/600px-Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diego-homem-black-sea-ancient-map-1559.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A medieval map of the Black Sea by
         <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Homem" title="Diogo Homem">
          Diogo Homem
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="1280" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg/300px-Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg/450px-Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg/600px-Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greek_colonies_of_the_Euxine_Sea.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Greek colonies (8th–3rd century BCE) of the Black Sea (Euxine, or "hospitable" sea).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Black Sea was a busy waterway on the crossroads of the ancient world: the Balkans to the west, the Eurasian
       <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">
        steppes
       </a>
       to the north, Caucasus and Central Asia to the east, Asia Minor and Mesopotamia to the south, and Greece to the south-west.
      </p>
      <p>
       The oldest processed gold in the world was found in Varna, and the Black Sea was supposedly sailed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Argonauts" title="Argonauts">
        Argonauts
       </a>
       . The land at the eastern end of the Black Sea,
       <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">
        Colchis
       </a>
       , (now
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">
        Georgia
       </a>
       ), marked for the Greeks the edge of the known world.
      </p>
      <p>
       The steppes to the north of the Black Sea have been suggested as the original homeland (
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Urheimat" title="Urheimat">
           Urheimat
          </a>
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) of the speakers of the
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European_language" title="Proto-Indo-European language">
        Proto-Indo-European language
       </a>
       , (PIE) the progenitor of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European language
       </a>
       family, by some scholars such as
       <a href="/wiki/Marija_Gimbutas" title="Marija Gimbutas">
        Marija Gimbutas
       </a>
       ; others move the heartland further east towards the
       <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">
        Caspian Sea
       </a>
       , yet others to
       <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">
        Anatolia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Black Sea became an
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Navy" title="Ottoman Navy">
        Ottoman Navy
       </a>
       lake within five years of
       <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">
        Genoa
       </a>
       losing the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean_Peninsula" title="Crimean Peninsula">
        Crimea
       </a>
       in 1479, after which the only Western merchant vessels to sail its waters were those of
       <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">
        Venice
       </a>
       's old rival
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ragusa" title="Republic of Ragusa">
        Ragusa
       </a>
       . This restriction was gradually changed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">
        Russian Navy
       </a>
       from 1783 until the relaxation of export controls in 1789 because of the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">
        French Revolution
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Black Sea was a significant naval theatre of
       <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare_of_World_War_I#Black_Sea" title="Naval warfare of World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       and saw both naval and land battles during
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">
        World War II
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Archaeology">
        Archaeology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Archaeology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="2299" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg/250px-Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg/375px-Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg/500px-Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aivazovsky_-_Black_Sea_Fleet_in_the_Bay_of_Theodosia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Aivazovsky" title="Ivan Aivazovsky">
          Ivan Aivazovsky
         </a>
         .
         <i>
          Black Sea Fleet in the Bay of Theodosia
         </i>
         , just before the
         <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">
          Crimean War
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ancient trade routes in the region are currently
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2015)">
           when?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       being extensively studied by scientists, as the Black Sea was sailed by
       <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">
        Hittites
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carians" title="Carians">
        Carians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">
        Colchians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Thracians" title="Thracians">
        Thracians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greeks" title="Ancient Greeks">
        Greeks
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Persians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">
        Cimmerians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
        Scythians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">
        Romans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greeks" title="Byzantine Greeks">
        Byzantines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">
        Goths
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">
        Huns
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avars_(Carpathians)" title="Avars (Carpathians)">
        Avars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">
        Bulgars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">
        Slavs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Varangians" title="Varangians">
        Varangians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusaders" title="Crusaders">
        Crusaders
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">
        Venetians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">
        Genoese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">
        Lithuanians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colchis" title="Colchis">
        Georgians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">
        Poles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">
        Tatars
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ottomans" title="Ottomans">
        Ottomans
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">
        Russians
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Perhaps the most promising areas in deepwater archaeology are the quest for submerged prehistoric settlements in the continental shelf and for ancient shipwrecks in the anoxic zone, which are expected to be exceptionally well preserved due to the absence of oxygen. This concentration of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_powers" title="Historical powers">
        historical powers
       </a>
       , combined with the preservative qualities of the deep
       <a href="/wiki/Anoxic_waters" title="Anoxic waters">
        anoxic waters
       </a>
       of the Black Sea, has attracted increased interest from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_archaeology" title="Marine archaeology">
        marine archaeologists
       </a>
       who have begun to discover a large number of
       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Black_Sea_shipwrecks" title="Ancient Black Sea shipwrecks">
        ancient ships and organic remains
       </a>
       in a high state of preservation.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_use">
        Modern use
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Modern use">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG/220px-Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG/330px-Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG/440px-Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Widok_na_Ja%C5%82t%C4%99_ze_statku_06.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Yalta" title="Yalta">
          Yalta
         </a>
         , Crimea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amasra,_Bart%C4%B1n,_Turkey.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Amasra%2C_Bart%C4%B1n%2C_Turkey.jpg/220px-Amasra%2C_Bart%C4%B1n%2C_Turkey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Amasra%2C_Bart%C4%B1n%2C_Turkey.jpg/330px-Amasra%2C_Bart%C4%B1n%2C_Turkey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Amasra%2C_Bart%C4%B1n%2C_Turkey.jpg/440px-Amasra%2C_Bart%C4%B1n%2C_Turkey.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amasra,_Bart%C4%B1n,_Turkey.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Amasra" title="Amasra">
          Amasra
         </a>
         , Turkey, is located on a small island in the Black Sea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_and_civic_use">
        Commercial and civic use
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Commercial and civic use">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       According to NATO, the Black sea is a strategic corridor that provides smuggling channels for moving legal and illegal goods including drugs, radioactive materials, and counterfeit goods that can be used to finance terrorism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Black_Sea_Security_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Black_Sea_Security-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Navigation">
        Navigation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Navigation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ports_and_ferry_terminals">
        Ports and ferry terminals
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ports and ferry terminals">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Transport_Workers%27_Federation" title="International Transport Workers' Federation">
        International Transport Workers' Federation
       </a>
       2013 study, there were at least 30 operating merchant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaport" title="Seaport">
        seaports
       </a>
       in the Black Sea (including at least 12 in
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Черное_море_признано_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Черное_море_признано-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Merchant_fleet_and_traffic">
        Merchant fleet and traffic
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Merchant fleet and traffic">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       According to the International Transport Workers' Federation 2013 study, there were around 2,400 commercial vessels operating in the Black Sea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Черное_море_признано_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Черное_море_признано-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fishing">
        Fishing
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Fishing">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/European_anchovy" title="European anchovy">
        Anchovy
       </a>
       : the Turkish commercial fishing fleet catches around 300,000 tons per year on average, and fishery carried out mainly in winter and the highest portion of the stock is caught between November and December.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrocarbons_exploration">
        Hydrocarbons exploration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hydrocarbons exploration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Since the 1980s, the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       started
       <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">
        offshore drilling
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        petroleum
       </a>
       in the sea's western portion (adjoining
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       's coast). The independent Ukraine continued and intensified that effort within its
       <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">
        exclusive economic zone
       </a>
       , inviting major international oil companies for exploration. Discovery of the new, massive oilfields in the area stimulated an influx of foreign investments. It also provoked a short-term peaceful
       <a href="/wiki/Territorial_dispute" title="Territorial dispute">
        territorial dispute
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       which was resolved in 2011 by an international court redefining the exclusive economic zones between the two countries.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Holiday_resorts_and_spas">
        Holiday resorts and spas
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Holiday resorts and spas">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cities_of_the_Black_Sea.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="514" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Cities_of_the_Black_Sea.png/350px-Cities_of_the_Black_Sea.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/Cities_of_the_Black_Sea.png 1.5x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cities_of_the_Black_Sea.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cities of the Black Sea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the years following the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       , the popularity of the Black Sea as a
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
        tourist
       </a>
       destination steadily increased. Tourism at Black Sea resorts became one of the region's growth industries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The following is a list of notable Black Sea
       <a href="/wiki/Resort" title="Resort">
        resort
       </a>
       towns:

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_military_use">
        Modern military use
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Modern military use">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="International_and_military_use_of_the_Straits">
        International and military use of the Straits
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Black_Sea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: International and military use of the Straits">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montreux_Convention_Regarding_the_Regime_of_the_Turkish_Straits" title="Montreux Convention Regarding the Regime of the Turkish Straits">
        1936 Montreux Convention
       </a>
       provides for a free passage of civilian ships between the international waters of the Black and the Mediterranean Seas. However, a single country (Turkey) has a complete control over the straits connecting the two seas. The 1982 amendments to the Montreux Convention allow Turkey to close the Straits at its discretion in both wartime and peacetime.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1936 Montreux Convention governs the passage of vessels between the Black and the Mediterranean Seas and the presence of military vessels belonging to non-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Littoral" title="Littoral">
        littoral
       </a>
       states in the Black Sea waters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
